With both pregnancies, she developed [placenta accreta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Placenta_accreta "Placenta accreta") after delivery, eventually undergoing surgery to remove the placenta and scar tissue.[\[267\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-268)[\[268\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-abc-pregnancy-269) After her second pregnancy, doctors advised her not to become pregnant again;[\[269\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-270) her third and fourth children were born via [surrogacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surrogacy "Surrogacy").[\[268\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-abc-pregnancy-269)[\[270\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-271)

Kardashian has also spoken about her [psoriasis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psoriasis "Psoriasis").[\[271\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-272) In May 2021, it was reported that Kardashian had tested positive for [COVID-19](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/COVID-19 "COVID-19") in November 2020. She confirmed this report[\[272\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-273) but denied reports that she caught the disease after hosting a party at a private island.[\[273\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-274)

In October 2025, Kardashian revealed that she received a [brain aneurysm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brain_aneurysm "Brain aneurysm") diagnosis and suggested the condition was due to the ongoing stress in dealing with splitting from West.[\[274\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-275)

### Wealth

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Kim_Kardashian_5%2C_2012.jpg/500px-Kim_Kardashian_5%2C_2012.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kim_Kardashian_5,_2012.jpg) Kardashian in Australia for an _[E! News](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/E!_News "E! News")_ event in 2012

In May 2014, Kardashian was estimated to be worth US$45million.[\[275\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-WealthEstimate-276) In 2015, _[Forbes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forbes "Forbes")_ reported she had "made more this year than ever as her earnings nearly doubled to $53 million from 2014's $28 million", and reported that she "has monetized fame better than any other".[\[276\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-277) Much of her income in the early-to-mid 2010s included wholesale earnings of the [Sears](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sears "Sears") line, the Kardashian Kollection, which brought in $600 million in 2013 and the Kardashian Beauty cosmetics line, Kardashian-branded tanning products, the boutique-line Dash, as well as sponsored social media posts which are collectively worth $300,000–500,000 per post.[\[277\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-278)[\[278\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-279)As of July 2018[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kim_Kardashian&action=edit), Kardashian was worth US$350 million.[\[279\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-280) She does not receive [alimony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alimony "Alimony") payments from either of her first two marriages.[\[280\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-281) Kardashian became a billionaire in April 2021[\[281\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-282) thanks to her shapewear company Skims, KKW Beauty, reality television, endorsements, and investments. _[Forbes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forbes "Forbes")_ has estimated her net worth at $1.7billion as of December 2024[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kim_Kardashian&action=edit),[\[282\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-283) making her one of the world's [wealthiest celebrities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_celebrities_by_net_worth "List of celebrities by net worth").

Kardashian has been included in the [_Forbes_ Celebrity 100](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forbes_Celebrity_100 "Forbes Celebrity 100") multiple times, which ranks the highest-earning celebrities annually. She first appeared on the list in 2012 as the seventh-highest-paid celebrity that year, with earnings of $18million.[\[283\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-284) In 2016, Kardashian was the 42nd-highest-paid celebrity with $51million; 40 percent of her earnings that year were from her mobile game _Kim Kardashian: Hollywood_.[\[284\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-285) In 2017, 2018, and 2019, she was ranked number 47, 30, and 26 with $45.5million,[\[285\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-286) $67million,[\[286\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-287) and $72million;[\[287\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-288) the last of which is her highest reported annual earnings. She was ranked the 48th-highest-paid celebrity of 2020, with $49.5million in earnings, majorly from her cosmetics line KKW Beauty, which generated $100million in sales the previous year.[\[288\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-289) Kardashian is among the ten highest-paid individuals on Instagram. As of 2023[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Kim_Kardashian&action=edit), she earns over $1.68million per sponsored Instagram post.[\[289\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-290) She was the twelfth-highest-paid celebrity on Instagram in 2024, with earnings of over $4.37 million across sponsored posts.[\[290\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-291)

### Legal controversy

In 2011, Kardashian filed a $20 million lawsuit against clothing retailer [Old Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Navy "Old Navy") after it aired an advertisement starring [Melissa Molinaro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melissa_Molinaro "Melissa Molinaro"). Kardashian alleged that Old Navy had misappropriated her likeness by featuring Molinaro, who looks like Kardashian, in the advertisement. Kardashian and [Gap](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gap_Inc. "Gap Inc."), Old Navy's parent company, settled for an undisclosed amount by August 2012.[\[291\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-292)

### Paris robbery

On October 2, 2016, while attending [Paris Fashion Week](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Fashion_Week "Paris Fashion Week"), Kardashian was [robbed at gunpoint](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robbery "Robbery") in the apartment where she was staying. Five individuals, dressed as police officers, bound and gagged her, then stole $10 million worth of jewelry.[\[292\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-293) The thieves got in her residence by threatening the concierge. Once they accessed Kardashian's room, they held a gun to her head and ordered her to give them her ring, then bound her wrists and legs with zip ties and wrapped duct tape around her eyes and mouth.[\[293\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-294)[\[294\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-295) Kardashian, who was placed in the bathtub, was physically unharmed and reportedly begged for her life.[\[295\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-296)[\[296\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-297)[\[297\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-298) She managed to wriggle her hands free from the zip ties on her wrists and scream for help. The thieves, after finding her jewelry box, promptly escaped.[\[298\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-299) On October 6, 2016, it was revealed that filming for the next season of _[Keeping Up with the Kardashians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keeping_Up_with_the_Kardashians "Keeping Up with the Kardashians")_ had been placed "on hold indefinitely" after the robbery.[\[299\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-300)

After the robbery was announced, several critics expressed skepticism about whether it was staged or not, with some even drawing comparison to Olympic swimmer [Ryan Lochte's recent false robbery claim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lochtegate "Lochtegate").[\[300\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-301)[\[301\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-302) On October 10, 2016, a video was released showing Kardashian immediately after the robbery, as police began conducting their investigation. In the video, she is seen using the cell phone that she had reported stolen, and did not have any of the markings she claimed from being bound by her captors, prompting more questions as to whether or not the events were staged.[\[302\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-303) In response, Kardashian filed lawsuits against several media outlets the following day, and secured a gag order to get the video removed from any articles due to it being part of an active police investigation.[\[303\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-304)[\[304\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-305)[\[305\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-306) On October 25, 2016, Kardashian dropped the lawsuit.[\[306\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-307)[\[307\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-308) Production resumed on _Keeping Up with the Kardashians_ on October 26.[\[308\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-309)

On January 9, 2017, French police detained 17 persons of interest for questioning in the robbery case.[\[309\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-310) Later in 2017, 16 people were arrested for their alleged involvement.[\[310\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-311) It was revealed in 2020 that French prosecutors would seek trial for 12 of the suspects.[\[311\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-312) The suspects who allegedly entered her room were of, or near, [senior](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senior_citizen "Senior citizen") age and were named the 'Grandpa Robbers' by the press.[\[312\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-313)

In April 2025, the case finally came to trial, with Kardashian giving evidence in person.[\[313\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-314) Eight of the defendants were convicted and two were acquitted.[\[314\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-315)

## Activism

During an interview with [Caity Weaver](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caity_Weaver "Caity Weaver") of _[GQ](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GQ "GQ")_ for the July 2016 issue, Kardashian described herself as a [Democrat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States) "Democratic Party (United States)"), and declared her support for [Hillary Clinton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hillary_Clinton "Hillary Clinton") in the [2016 U.S. presidential election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_U.S._presidential_election "2016 U.S. presidential election").[\[315\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-316)[\[316\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-317)

In January 2017, she [tweeted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tweeted "Tweeted") a table of statistics that went viral, highlighting statistics that show that [gun violence in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gun_violence_in_the_United_States "Gun violence in the United States") kills 11,737 people annually while [terrorism in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terrorism_in_the_United_States "Terrorism in the United States") kills 14 people annually. In December 2017, the tweet was mentioned by the [Royal Statistical Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Statistical_Society "Royal Statistical Society") in the announcement of its "International Statistic of the Year" for 2017.[\[317\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-318)[\[318\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-weforum-319) On a trip to Uganda in October 2018, she and her husband met with President [Yoweri Museveni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoweri_Museveni "Yoweri Museveni"). They had a press conference, and Kanye talked about [tourism in Uganda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tourism_in_Uganda "Tourism in Uganda"). They were criticized for meeting Museveni due to his then-recent crackdown on the opposition and the [Ugandan LGBT community](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Uganda "LGBT rights in Uganda").[\[319\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-320)[\[320\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-321)[\[321\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-322)

In April 2019, _[Vogue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vogue_(magazine) "Vogue (magazine)")_ reported that Kardashian was studying to pass the [bar exam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bar_examination "Bar examination"); instead of attending [law school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_school "Law school"), she is [reading law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reading_law "Reading law").[\[322\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-323) In 2021, Kardashian said she had failed her first-year law exam (the [baby bar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_Bar_of_California#Law_Office_Study_Program "State Bar of California")) for a second time, performing "slightly worse" than her first attempt earlier in the year.[\[323\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-324)[\[324\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-325) In December 2021, she passed the "baby bar" law exam on her fourth attempt.[\[325\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-fourth_attempt-326) She completed her law reader program in 2025, but in November 2025, announced she failed her first attempt at the bar exam.[\[326\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-327)[\[13\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-NW-bar-fail-13)

In 2020, Kardashian condemned the actions of [Azerbaijan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azerbaijan "Azerbaijan") in the [2020 Nagorno-Karabakh conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_Nagorno-Karabakh_conflict "2020 Nagorno-Karabakh conflict"), and expressed her support for Armenia and the [Republic of Artsakh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Artsakh "Republic of Artsakh").[\[327\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-328)[\[328\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-329) On November 20, 2021, it was reported that Kardashian and the English soccer club [Leeds United F.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C. "Leeds United F.C."), with the help of Rabbi Moshe Margertten of the Tzedek Association,[\[329\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-330) had financially helped [female Afghan soccer players](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women's_football_in_Afghanistan "Women's football in Afghanistan") to make their way safely to England. The women and girls had escaped Afghanistan following the [Taliban](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taliban "Taliban") takeover, but were stranded in Pakistan.[\[330\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-331)[\[331\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-332)

### Armenian genocide recognition

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Kim_Kardashian_in_front_of_the_Armenian_Genocide_Memorial_in_2019.jpg/500px-Kim_Kardashian_in_front_of_the_Armenian_Genocide_Memorial_in_2019.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Kim_Kardashian_in_front_of_the_Armenian_Genocide_Memorial_in_2019.jpg) Kardashian at the [Armenian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide "Armenian genocide") [memorial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsitsernakaberd "Tsitsernakaberd") in [Yerevan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yerevan "Yerevan"), Armenia in October 2019

Kardashian has expressed pride in her Armenian and Scottish ancestry.[\[332\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-333)[\[333\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-334) She is not a citizen of either [Armenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenia "Armenia") or the United Kingdom, and does not speak Armenian.[\[334\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-335) She has advocated for the [recognition of the Armenian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide_recognition "Armenian genocide recognition") on numerous occasions and encouraged President [Barack Obama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barack_Obama "Barack Obama") and the United States government to consider its acknowledgement.[\[335\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-336)[\[336\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-337)[\[337\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-338) In April 2016, Kardashian wrote an article on her website condemning _[The Wall Street Journal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal "The Wall Street Journal")_ for running an advertisement by [FactCheckArmenia.com](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FactCheckArmenia.com "FactCheckArmenia.com") [denying the Armenian genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide_denial "Armenian genocide denial").[\[338\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-339) In April 2021, Kardashian wrote a letter to President [Joe Biden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joe_Biden "Joe Biden") thanking him for officially recognizing the Armenian genocide and becoming the first United States president ever to do so.[\[339\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-340)[\[340\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-341)

In April 2015, Kardashian traveled to Armenia with her husband, her sister Khloé, and her eldest daughter and visited the Armenian Genocide Memorial [Tsitsernakaberd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsitsernakaberd "Tsitsernakaberd") in [Yerevan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yerevan "Yerevan").[\[341\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-342) On October 10, 2020, Kardashian announced she donated $1 million to [Armenia Fund](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenia_Fund "Armenia Fund"), a humanitarian organization that supports Armenia's development.[\[342\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-343)[\[343\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-344)

### Prison reform and clemency advocacy

Kardashian has worked in the area of prison reform, advocating for the commutation of the sentence of Chris Young and also of [Alice Marie Johnson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alice_Marie_Johnson "Alice Marie Johnson"), a woman who received a life sentence for a first-time drug offense as the leader of a major cocaine ring in Tennessee[\[344\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-yahoo.com-345)[\[345\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-CBS-346)[\[346\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-AP1997-347) which was granted by President [Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump") in June 2018.[\[347\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-348)[\[348\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-349) Along with [Van Jones](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Van_Jones "Van Jones") and [Jared Kushner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jared_Kushner "Jared Kushner"), she was instrumental in persuading President Trump to support the [First Step Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Step_Act "First Step Act"), which enacted major reforms in the US prison system. Van Jones later stated that without Kardashian, the act would have never passed because it would not have received the president's support. It was later passed by a great majority in the [US Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate "United States Senate").[\[349\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-350)[\[350\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-351)[\[351\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-352)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/President_Trump_Meets_with_Sentencing_Commutation_Recipients_%2849624188912%29.jpg/500px-President_Trump_Meets_with_Sentencing_Commutation_Recipients_%2849624188912%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:President_Trump_Meets_with_Sentencing_Commutation_Recipients_(49624188912).jpg) Kardashian (second from right) welcomes sentence commutation recipients with President [Donald Trump](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donald_Trump "Donald Trump"), 2018

In 2019, Kardashian largely funded the 90 Days to Freedom campaign, an initiative to release nonviolent drug offenders from life sentences by attorneys [Brittany K. Barnett](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brittany_K._Barnett "Brittany K. Barnett") and MiAngel Cody.[\[352\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-Johnson-353) The effort resulted in 17 persons being released under provisions of the [First Step Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Step_Act "First Step Act").[\[352\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-Johnson-353) Kardashian was widely credited for the success of the campaign in media headlines.[\[353\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-354) Commentary on her involvement ranged from praise, to assertions that it was a public relations stunt, to accusations that she was taking the credit for work she did not do.[\[352\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-Johnson-353) In a Facebook post from May 7 of that year, Barnett commented on the divisive and underfunded nature of the "criminal justice reform space", adding, "Kim linked arms with us to support us when foundations turned us down. We and our clients and their families have a lot of love for her and are deeply grateful for her."[\[354\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-BKBFB-355)[\[355\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-WILLIAM_COWEN-356)

In April 2022, Kardashian advocated for the clemency of [Melissa Lucio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melissa_Lucio "Melissa Lucio"), the only woman of Hispanic descent on Texas' death row, in a series of tweets. She tweeted, "I recently just read about the case of Melissa Lucio and wanted to share her story with you. She has been on death row for over 14 years for her daughter's death that was a tragic accident."[\[356\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-Remezcla_death_row-357)[\[357\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-independent_death_row-358) Lucio is on death row for the abuse and death of her daughter, who was two years old. Kardashian deleted the series of tweets the same day.[\[356\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-Remezcla_death_row-357) When Lucio was granted a [stay of execution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stay_of_execution "Stay of execution") on April 25, Kardashian celebrated on her social media channels.[\[358\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-stay_of_execution-359)

In July 2022, Kardashian expressed support and petitioned for the release of rapper [Gunna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gunna_(rapper) "Gunna (rapper)"), who was imprisoned without bond, charged with one count of violating the [Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Racketeer_Influenced_and_Corrupt_Organizations_Act "Racketeer Influenced and Corrupt Organizations Act").[\[359\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-Gunna-360) However, in October of the same year, Gunna was again denied release from jail ahead of his January trial.[\[360\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-361) In December, Gunna pled guilty to a single charge of racketeering and was sentenced to five years in prison, with one year commuted to time served and the rest of the sentence suspended subject to probation conditions. He was soon released from jail, and instead was ordered to serve 500 hours of [community service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Community_service "Community service").[\[361\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-362)[\[362\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-363)

In December 2023, Kardashian publicly expressed her belief in the innocence of Alabama prisoner [Toforest Johnson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toforest_Johnson "Toforest Johnson"), who has been on death row for more than 25 years despite calls for his conviction to be overturned from the original trial prosecutor in his case and the current District Attorney, [Danny Carr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Danny_Carr "Danny Carr").[\[363\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-364) Kardashian posted about Johnson's case on her Instagram account, asking "Who is Toforest Johnson? And why does the state of Alabama have an innocent man on death row?"[\[364\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-365) She added a link to _[Earwitness](https://www.toforestjohnson.com/podcast),_ a serial podcast about Johnson's case and also to an advocacy [website](https://www.toforestjohnson.com/) that contains more information about Johnson's case. Kardashian spoke out about Johnson's case again in March and April 2024, when she posted a video of Johnson's daughter Akeriya Terry on her Instagram account.[\[365\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-366) Johnson remains on Alabama's death row and no execution date has yet been set.[\[366\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-367)

In September 2024, Kardashian visited convicted murderers [Lyle and Erik Menendez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyle_and_Erik_Menendez "Lyle and Erik Menendez") along with over 30 other inmates at the [Richard J. Donovan Correctional Facility](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Richard_J._Donovan_Correctional_Facility "Richard J. Donovan Correctional Facility").[\[367\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-:0-368) The meeting focused on prison reform, which included a discussion of the Green Space Project, a prison beautification initiative led by Lyle Menendez.[\[368\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-:1-369) Accompanying Kardashian during the visit were her sister [Khloé Kardashian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khlo%C3%A9_Kardashian "Khloé Kardashian"), mother [Kris Jenner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kris_Jenner "Kris Jenner"), film producer [Scott Budnick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scott_Budnick_(film_producer) "Scott Budnick (film producer)"), actor [Cooper Koch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cooper_Koch "Cooper Koch")—who portrayed Erik in the [Netflix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netflix "Netflix") limited series _[Monsters: The Lyle and Erik Menendez Story](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monsters:_The_Lyle_and_Erik_Menendez_Story "Monsters: The Lyle and Erik Menendez Story")_—and Koch's partner, filmmaker [Stuart McClave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stuart_McClave "Stuart McClave").[\[367\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-:0-368)[\[368\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-:1-369) In October of that year, Kardashian penned an essay for [NBC News](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NBC_News "NBC News") in which she advocated for the brothers' release, arguing that they were "not monsters" and had been failed by a justice system that did not adequately account for their alleged abuse or their subsequent rehabilitation.[\[369\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-370) The release of the essay coincided with a renewed legal review of the case by the [Los Angeles County District Attorney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_County_District_Attorney "Los Angeles County District Attorney")'s office.[\[370\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-371) In May 2025, a judge resentenced the brothers to 50 years to life, making them eligible for parole under California law because they were under 26 years old at the time of the murders.[\[371\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-372) On August 21, 2025, Erik was denied parole by the California Board of Parole Hearings, which cited ongoing rule violations and concerns regarding public safety.[\[372\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-373) Lyle was also denied parole the following day, with the board referencing repeated infractions involving the possession of a cell phone.[\[373\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-:2-374) Both brothers are scheduled to be eligible for a second parole hearing in 2028, though they may become eligible as early as 18 months after the initial hearing provided they maintain a clean disciplinary record.[\[373\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-:2-374)

## Notes

1. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_ref-20)In 2015, Jenner changed her first name to Caitlyn after a [gender transition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_transition "Gender transition").[\[19\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-19)
2. [1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_ref-with_377-0) [2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_ref-with_377-1) [3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_ref-with_377-2)With [Kourtney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kourtney_Kardashian "Kourtney Kardashian"), [Khloé](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khlo%C3%A9_Kardashian "Khloé Kardashian"), [Rob](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rob_Kardashian "Rob Kardashian") and [Kris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kris_Jenner "Kris Jenner").
3. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_ref-382)Prior to her [gender transition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_transitioning "Gender transitioning"), [Caitlyn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caitlyn_Jenner "Caitlyn Jenner") went by her [birth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Birth_name "Birth name") [middle name](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_name "Middle name") Bruce.
4. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_ref-383)With [Kourtney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kourtney_Kardashian "Kourtney Kardashian"), [Khloé](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khlo%C3%A9_Kardashian "Khloé Kardashian"), [Rob](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rob_Kardashian "Rob Kardashian"), [Kris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kris_Jenner "Kris Jenner"), [Kendall](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kendall_Jenner "Kendall Jenner"), [Kylie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kylie_Jenner "Kylie Jenner") and [Bruce](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caitlyn_Jenner "Caitlyn Jenner").[\[c\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kim_Kardashian#cite_note-382)
